class="ds-flex ds-items-center ds-space-x-4"><a href="/team/tamil-nadu-2133" class=""><img width="24" height="24" alt="Tamil Nadu (and Madras) logo" style="width:24px;height:24px" class="!ds-text-typo-paragraph ds-text-ui-typo ds-underline ds-underline-offset-4 ds-decoration-ui-stroke hover:ds-text-ui-typo-primary hover:ds-decoration-ui-stroke-primary ds-block"><span class="ds-text-title-s ds-font-bold">Tamil Nadu</span></a></span></div></div><div class="ds-relative ds-overflow-hidden ds-mt-6" style="height:112px"><div class="ci-player-bio-content"><p>Like R Ashwin from Tamil Nadu before him, Washington Sundar went from being a batsman as a youngster to making his name as an offspinner. After representing India at the 2016 Under-19 World Cup, he replaced Ashwin at Rising Pune Supergiant in the 2017 IPL, and bowled at an impressive economy rate to help his side to the final.</p><p>Sundar's father, a cricketer who made it to the Tamil Nadu Ranji probables without getting into the final squad, named him Washington to honour his godfather, Mr Washington, who would buy bats for him and pay his fees. Sundar loved to bowl but only in matches because he found it boring to just field. He eventually started to take it seriously under the eye of former India offspiner M Venkataramana. Sundar bowls with great discipline, and held his own in domestic one-day competitions and after making his Twenty20 debut as a 17-year-old in the IPL.
